<div id="review_114051282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114051282" />
    <a title="Traveller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3145526-traveller"><img alt="Traveller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423246742p2/3145526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114051282?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Traveller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Traveller" href="/user/show/3145526-traveller">Traveller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114051282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5857758749549408781">Though a reasonably good piece for a teenager to have written (apparently King started writing this as a teenager), a lot of immaturity still shows through.<br/><br/>Despite the fact that I could not manage to build up any empathy with the main character (the killer) Charlie Decker, Charlie simply seemed too normal in his general thought processes to appear phsychotic. He simply came across as a spoilt, extremely immature kid - a product of the typical syndrome of the military father and over-indulgent mo</span>
  <span id="freeText5857758749549408781" style="display:none">Though a reasonably good piece for a teenager to have written (apparently King started writing this as a teenager), a lot of immaturity still shows through.<br /><br />Despite the fact that I could not manage to build up any empathy with the main character (the killer) Charlie Decker, Charlie simply seemed too normal in his general thought processes to appear phsychotic. He simply came across as a spoilt, extremely immature kid - a product of the typical syndrome of the military father and over-indulgent mother. Many families function like this, though very few of the kids from such families actually pick up guns and go around shooting people, or clobber people over the head with wrenches; indeed - most kids show some resilience - so basically this is a person with no phsychological reserves.<br />He doesn't seem to quite fit 100% into a pshychopath mold either; - so I'm not sure where King was going (or trying to go) with this character. <br /><br />In fact, it would seem that King is trying to talk out against discipline, and at the same time condoning hooliganism and destructive behaviour, not to mention murder and violence.<br /><br />I felt a lot more empathy for the real victim in the story, Ted Jones. The way he is tortured and victimised by the mob on both a psychological and a physical level, left me a with an extremely bad taste in the mouth - was this supposed to be a modern version of aspects of Lord of the Flies?<br /><br />A lot of the dialogue came across as pretty unrealistic of how people would talk in a crisis situation like this one. Especially the story that Decker recounts of his sexual misadventure while under the influence of marijuana, seemed like a streamlined and polished retelling of an event by a professional writer - and not what must have been a painful recollection of a relatively traumatic (or frustrating and embarassing at the least) event by a teenage boy.<br /><br />All in all, although the book was an easy read due to King's very accessible style, (and definitely an infinitely more gripping read than Catcher in the Rye), I'm giving it only 2 stars due to the plain mean-spiritedness of character that shines through on every page, not to mention the trivialisation of (and even glimmers of glorification of) cruelty and violence.<br /><br />EDIT: I've slept on it, and I think I need to downgrade my rating to a 1. The more I think of the callous way that the subject of the death of 2 teachers and torture of an already beleaugered boy is treated, the more I want to give the book a zero.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5857758749549408781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_52525022" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52525022" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52525022?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52525022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8704304647679234934">This is a really eye-opening story, and it's really not hard to understand why King would have wanted to pull this from circulation. I'm sure that this story is terrifying in the same way that <i>Misery</i> is terrifying: It could really happen. But this is even worse, because not only is it possible, it's happened. This is close to home. That makes it truly terrifying. <br/><br/>But I have to say that the story was less about the fact that Charlie Decker brought a gun to school and used it, and more about who C</span>
  <span id="freeText8704304647679234934" style="display:none">This is a really eye-opening story, and it's really not hard to understand why King would have wanted to pull this from circulation. I'm sure that this story is terrifying in the same way that <i>Misery</i> is terrifying: It could really happen. But this is even worse, because not only is it possible, it's happened. This is close to home. That makes it truly terrifying. <br /><br />But I have to say that the story was less about the fact that Charlie Decker brought a gun to school and used it, and more about who Charlie was and why he wound up where he did. This story is almost a PSA on parent/teen relations. At least, I saw it that way, but I'm not a parent yet. <br /><br />I loved that the kids in Charlie's class were so open and honest with each other, with the exception of Ted. I was left wondering what exactly happened to Ted, both behind closed doors while in the classroom and afterward, but it's not hard to make an educated guess. It was almost ritualistic, and I felt that the students were sort of cleansing away his barriers to allow Ted to be honest with himself about who he is. This in itself makes the story great. <br /><br />This is a hard one to find in print, but luckily I was able to find a used copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10617.The_Bachman_Books_Four_Early_Novels_by_Richard_Bachman__Rage___The_Long_Walk___Roadwork___The_Running_Man_" title="The Bachman Books Four Early Novels by Richard Bachman (Rage / The Long Walk / Roadwork / The Running Man) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bachman Books: Four Early Novels by Richard Bachman</a> which contained the story. Also, there is an audio version floating around out there, but I wasn't terribly impressed with it. I would recommend it though, if you're unable to find the story in print. It's worth the read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8704304647679234934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15316624528406889237"><br/>I’m not sure how to review this book, because I liked it and yet I didn’t.<br/><br/>It’s a short, quick read and well written considering it’s King’s first book, but I found it unpleasant and bleak.   <span id="freeText15316624528406889237" style="display:none"><br />I’m not sure how to review this book, because I liked it and yet I didn’t.<br /><br />It’s a short, quick read and well written considering it’s King’s first book, but I found it unpleasant and bleak. It reminded me a little of Lord of the Flies.<br /><br />The story dragged through the middle and I had to force myself to keep reading. <br /><br />What made it bearable was that I enjoyed the characters, with the exception of Charlie. He just wasn’t believable to me and I had to keep reminding myself that he was a teenager. He seemed much older.<br /><br />I liked the ending, which wasn’t what I expected.<br /><br />All in all it wasn’t bad, but it wasn’t great either. I won’t bother to read it again.<br /><br />***<br /><br />CONNECTIONS:<br /><br />High school teacher Jean Underwood shares her surname with Larry Underwood (The Stand)<br /><br />Richard Stark – The pseudonym of author Donald E Westlake. He shares the same surname with George Stark (The Dark Half)<br /><br />Pig Pen – There was also a student nicknamed Pig Pen in Cain Rose Up.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1864779185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864779185" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24668886-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381636198p2/24668886.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864779185?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/24668886-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24668886-scott?shelf=stephen-king-scary">stephen-king-scary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864779185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1797949352940524697">The Stephen King Goodreads Discussion Group is doing a re-read of his works from the beginning to the end. It’s been a long time since I have really immersed myself in Uncle Stevie’s world, but a rate of a book a month, I am all in. My goal is to read and review each one with as much honesty and reflection that I can give. <br/><br/>Background – “Rage” was the first novel by Stephen King published under the pseudonym of Richard Bachman, originally published back in 1977. Because the novel describes a scho</span>
  <span id="freeText1797949352940524697" style="display:none">The Stephen King Goodreads Discussion Group is doing a re-read of his works from the beginning to the end. It’s been a long time since I have really immersed myself in Uncle Stevie’s world, but a rate of a book a month, I am all in. My goal is to read and review each one with as much honesty and reflection that I can give. <br /><br />Background – “Rage” was the first novel by Stephen King published under the pseudonym of Richard Bachman, originally published back in 1977. Because the novel describes a school shooting, which is a rather sensitive topic, King allowed the novel to go out of print. The only primary way to read it is to find it in a used bookstore in either the individual form or in the omnibus version of “The Bachman Books”. Length-wise it is a short novel. My softcover omnibus paperback lists it as 131 pages. <br /><br />Plotline – This is a controversial story (in many regards) about a troubled high school senior, Charlie Everett Decker. Charlie is back in school following his suspension for striking his chemistry teacher with wrench, hospitalizing and nearly killing him. The story opens with Charlie having an explosive confrontation with the principal, retrieving a hidden pistol, setting his locker on fire, and returning to his algebra class where he shoots his teacher and takes the class hostage. <br />That’s just the beginning. The rest of the story plays out over the next several hours as the class takes part in their own twisted version of “The Breakfast Club”. As the police gather outside and try to take control of the situation, the students hold their own psychotherapy session as Charlie’s troubled past is revealed, including a warped relationship with his abusive father. <br /><br />Thoughts and Reflections – This book is full of raw emotional anger. It is told trough Charlie’s voice in a no hold’s barred style. As I read it again for the first time in many years, two primary thoughts struck me. First, it really feels like an eighteen- year old is telling the story. It’s disjointed, bounces around between the current action and impacting memories. Charlie is juvenile in his language and thoughts because that’s what he is. He comes across like a disturbed young man’s mindset would sound like. Second, one of King’s greatest strengths was letting his “inside” voice come out in his writing. He would say the things we think but never say or admit out loud. But I think King had an even angrier and sarcastic deeper voice that I will call his “inside inner” voice. I really feel like that writing books under the pseudonym of Richard Bachman was about King letting that “inside inner” voice (the one where we would never admit things to ourselves) come out full force like a fully pressured firehose. Writing as Bachman, King is dark, satirical, and downright angry about things. I would even venture to say these books might have been a cathartic and cleansing experience for him. <br /><br />Other Notes – This book was originally titled “Getting It On” but was change before being published to “Rage”. <br /><br />Overall – This is definitely a book that makes some strong statements. Still, you can tell King wrote it in his early years when he was still developing as a writer. There are some plot and character challenges, but it still holds up enough to create a strong emotional response from the reader no matter what your personal beliefs and philosophies are. It’s not a read for enjoyment sake, but rather one that makes you think about how family, friends, and social activities can influence your behavior and how you see yourself for good or for bad. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1797949352940524697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2444364458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2444364458" />
    <a title="Michela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7122120-michela"><img alt="Michela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600608907p2/7122120.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2444364458?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michela" href="/user/show/7122120-michela">Michela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/34812780-rage">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7122120-michela?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2444364458&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2444364458" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11507466183111446349">“When you're five and you hurt, you make a big noise in the world. At ten you whimper. But by the time you make fifteen you begin to eat the poisoned apples that grow on your own inner tree of pain.” <br/><br/>This is a story about rage, pain and mental disorder.<br/>Charlie Decker, a Maine high school senior, storms out of the principal office, retrieves a pistol from his locker, kills two teachers and takes all his classmates hostages. What's happening in Charlie's head? <br/><br/>The main theme of this novel is the p</span>
  <span id="freeText11507466183111446349" style="display:none">“When you're five and you hurt, you make a big noise in the world. At ten you whimper. But by the time you make fifteen you begin to eat the poisoned apples that grow on your own inner tree of pain.” <br /><br />This is a story about rage, pain and mental disorder.<br />Charlie Decker, a Maine high school senior, storms out of the principal office, retrieves a pistol from his locker, kills two teachers and takes all his classmates hostages. What's happening in Charlie's head? <br /><br />The main theme of this novel is the power struggle between a boy and the institutions, like the school, the family, religion and the police. Charlie is not a rebel, in his mind he just wants to change things that make him suffer, he wants to be the one who gives orders now. <br /><br />Stockholm syndrome kicks in and his classmates snap too, confessing to the other friends/hostages their deepest secrets: their sexual experiences, family problems, painful memories of their childhood. These kids are definitely not okay and Charlie is leading some sort of psychotherapy group, with terrible outcomes (which reminded me of Lord of the Flies).<br /><br />I'm impressed because Stephen King actually wrote Rage before Carrie, so he was very young, and this is such a cold and dark novel. Sadly, what happens in the book is not so far from reality. What I didn't like, because it's hardly plausible, is that in only a few hours the whole class became friend and accomplice of Charlie, who was target and victim of their bullying since then.<br /><br />This is the first book I read from the Bachman collection, hopefully I'll like the others more!<br />3 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11507466183111446349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2568058409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2568058409" />
    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2568058409?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568058409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1086189070604297848">I know there’s a lot of mixed reviews on this one so I was a bit wary going into it but they turned out to be unnecessary because I absolutely loved it! It’s such a dark and chilling story and it drew me right in and sunk its claws into me. I didn’t like our main character but I did absolutely LOVE to hate him and that’s almost better than loving and relating to a character. I will admit some parts were a teeny bit confusing but that’s only to be expected when the narrator is insane! </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_310652166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/310652166" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/310652166?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=drama-gen-fiction">drama-gen-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310652166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9165311199324817640"><b> “There's a Mr. Hyde for every happy Jekyll face, a dark face on the other side of the mirror.” </b><br/><br/>Rage is the ultimate in teenage angst, kind of like a more violent, twisted version of 'The Babysitter's Club' because of the morbid teenage bonding that went on inside the classroom. <br/><br/>An interesting book, glad I read it. It's not a typical school shooter type of fiction novel - and this alarming plot trope is why King banned publications of this book after that became an unfortunate "in" thing. The fi</span>
  <span id="freeText9165311199324817640" style="display:none"><b> “There's a Mr. Hyde for every happy Jekyll face, a dark face on the other side of the mirror.” </b><br /><br />Rage is the ultimate in teenage angst, kind of like a more violent, twisted version of 'The Babysitter's Club' because of the morbid teenage bonding that went on inside the classroom. <br /><br />An interesting book, glad I read it. It's not a typical school shooter type of fiction novel - and this alarming plot trope is why King banned publications of this book after that became an unfortunate "in" thing. The first half is more intriguing and a higher star rating - but by the end it sours a bit and became a little shaky. What I dug most was the unexpected bonding of most of the classmates, even if I felt bad for a particular character they kept picking on.<br /><br />It's short and most of the book is talking - not actually very violent outside the beginning - and there isn't a concrete reason given for the violence other than the character being unstable and super angsty. He makes Holden Caulfield appear almost optimistic.<br /><br />The ending shows that the bond went beyond the classroom, and that the teens persisted in thinking the adults were all artificial beings who couldn't possibly understand them. Charlie's character comes across convincing enough and we spend plenty of time in his head, but there still aren't any clear reasons or explanations for how he is, what he does, or what comes after the story. I guess maybe that's the point after all - some things aren't understandable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9165311199324817640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TLyypPSk1Kqik3HDhJATbhMjbui8JBRalgh3FVxmJiKA9JPqHqtEOmnPLMBvPGYacBsinLt8IUSt/z8aYBsBmQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PH24L60MHlY0QKqMHbJDuzoujya1eNL0fbvhoUHKMRvwNZlhRwOOxv8c94/2HjbPWRbDUrIg5+pGTKmufbcWoA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5858.Richard_Bachman">About Richard Bachman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5858.Richard_Bachman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1289702449p3/5858.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5858.Richard_Bachman">Richard Bachman
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,284
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14346043512825571997">This is a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King' title='Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stephen King</a> pseudonym.<br/><br/>At the beginning of Stephen King's career, the general view among publishers was that an author was limited to one book per year, since publishing more would be unacceptable to the public. King therefore wanted to write under another name, in order to increase his publication without over-saturating the market for the King "brand". He convinced his publisher, Signe</span>
  <span id="freeText14346043512825571997" style="display:none">This is a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a> pseudonym.<br /><br />At the beginning of Stephen King's career, the general view among publishers was that an author was limited to one book per year, since publishing more would be unacceptable to the public. King therefore wanted to write under another name, in order to increase his publication without over-saturating the market for the King "brand". He convinced his publisher, Signet Books, to print these novels under a pseudonym.<br /><br />In his introduction to <i>The Bachman Books</i>, King states that adopting the nom de plume Bachman was also an attempt to make sense out of his career and try to answer the question of whether his success was due to talent or luck. He says he deliberately released the Bachman novels with as little marketing presence as possible and did his best to "load the dice against" Bachman. King concludes that he has yet to find an answer to the "talent versus luck" question, as he felt he was outed as Bachman too early to know. The Bachman book <i>Thinner</i> (1984) sold 28,000 copies during its initial run—and then ten times as many when it was revealed that Bachman was, in fact, King.<br /><br />The pseudonym King originally selected (Gus Pillsbury) is King's maternal grandfather's name, but at the last moment King changed it to Richard Bachman. Richard is a tribute to crime author Donald E. Westlake's long-running pseudonym Richard Stark. (The surname Stark was later used in King's novel <i>The Dark Half</i>, in which an author's malevolent pseudonym, "George Stark", comes to life.) Bachman was inspired by Bachman–Turner Overdrive, a rock and roll band King was listening to at the time his publisher asked him to choose a pseudonym on the spot.<br /><br />King provided biographical details for Bachman, initially in the "about the author" blurbs in the early novels. Known "facts" about Bachman were that he was born in New York, served a four-year stint in the Coast Guard, which he then followed with ten years in the merchant marine. Bachman finally settled down in rural central New Hampshire, where he ran a medium-sized dairy farm, writing at night. His fifth novel was dedicated to his wife, Claudia Inez Bachman, who also received credit for the bogus author photo on the book jacket. Other "facts" about the author were revealed in publicity dispatches from Bachman's publishers: the Bachmans had one child, a boy, who died in an unfortunate, Stephen King-ish type accident at the age of six, when he fell through a well and drowned. In 1982, a brain tumour was discovered near the base of Bachman's brain; tricky surgery removed it. After Bachman's true identity was revealed, later publicity dispatches (and about the author blurbs) revealed that Bachman died suddenly in late 1985 of "cancer of the pseudonym, a rare form of schizonomia".<br /><br />King dedicated Bachman's early books—<i>Rage (1977), The Long Walk (1979), Roadwork (1981)</i>, and <i>The Running Man</i> (1982)—to people close to him. The link between King and his shadow writer was exposed after a Washington, D.C. bookstore clerk, Steve Brown, noted similarities between the writing styles of King and Bachman. Brown located publisher's records at the Library of Congress which included a document naming King as the author of one of Bachman's novels. Brown wrote to King's publishers with a copy of the documents he had uncovered, and asked them what to do. Two weeks later, King telephoned Brown personally and suggested he write an article about how he discovered the truth, allowing himself to be interviewed. King has taken full ownership of the Bachman name on numerous occasions, as with the republication of the first four Bachman titles as <i> The Bachman Books: Four Early Novels by Stephen King</i> in 1985. The introduction, titled "Why I Was Bachman," details the whole Bachman/King story.<br /><br />Source: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Bachmanhttps://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Bachman">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14346043512825571997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
